**Task Description:**
You are tasked with identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) from the user's input. This includes, but is not limited to:
- Full names (e.g., "Sandy", "Elenora", "Eleanora", "Salar", "Waqas")
- Business names, company names, or brand-specific terms (e.g., "Mishdad Beauty Website", "Stan Store")
- Email addresses
- Phone numbers
- Physical addresses
- Any other identifiers that could be used to trace back to an individual or organization

Replace such PII with generic placeholders that are clearly distinguishable from actual content (e.g., "[Name]", "[Company Name]", "[Email Address]", "[Department/Section Name]").

**Domain-Specific Considerations:**
- Be cautious of business names, product names, or brand-specific terms that may contain embedded PII or proprietary information.
- Preserve the structure of numbered lists, bullet points, and formatting (e.g., line breaks, `<br/>`, or markdown) to ensure the rewritten query remains functionally equivalent to the original.
- Identify and replace any PII that may be embedded within phrases (e.g., "South Western Railway" may be a specific entity and not PII, but "Covid-19 positive and negative impact on them" should remain unchanged if no PII is present).
- Maintain the original intent and meaning of the query, ensuring that the rewritten version can be used for the same purpose without revealing any private or sensitive information.
- If the input includes sections such as "SEO Tips," "How to Sell," "Platforms to Use," or "Instagram Keywords," ensure these sections are preserved in the rewritten query with PII removed or replaced as needed.

**Generalizable Strategy:**
- Scan the input for any terms that could be considered PII.
- Replace such terms with appropriate generic placeholders.
- Retain all non-PII content, including technical terms, marketing strategies, SEO tips, platform suggestions, and keywords.
- Ensure that the rewritten query is grammatically correct and semantically equivalent to the original.
- Double-check the output for any remaining PII that may have been overlooked, particularly in cases where the PII is not explicitly named (e.g., "them" in "Covid-19 positive and negative impact on them" should be left as-is if no PII is identified).

**Output Format:**
- Present the rewritten query in the same format as the original (e.g., numbered list, bullet points, paragraphs).
- Include any additional sections such as "SEO Tips," "How to Sell," "Platforms to Use," or "Instagram Keywords" if present in the original input.
- Ensure that all placeholders are clearly marked and distinguishable from actual content.
- Provide a brief explanation of the changes made if the original input included a request for an explanation (as seen in Example 3).

**Important Notes:**
- If the original input contains multiple names or entities, ensure each is replaced with a unique placeholder (e.g., "[Name 1]/[Name 2]").
- If the input is in a language other than English, ensure that PII is identified and replaced in that language as well.
- Avoid introducing new information or altering the intent of the original message beyond the removal of PII.
- Ensure that placeholders do not resemble real names, companies, or other PII in any way.

- The assistant must ensure that the anonymized query remains grammatically correct and semantically equivalent to the original, with no loss of clarity or intent.

Iteration 13: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Anonymize User Queries by Removing Personally Identifiable Information (PII)

## Input Format
The input is a text query or message provided by the user. This may include sentences, paragraphs, bullet points, headers, or other structured content. The task is to process this text and anonymize it by replacing all instances of PII with standardized placeholders.

---

## Task Description

You are to **anonymize a user's query by removing all personally identifiable information (PII)**, including but not limited to names, addresses, phone numbers, email addresses, URLs, company names, usernames, dates, locations, job reference numbers, and any other sensitive data. The anonymized text must **preserve the original meaning, intent, grammatical structure, and formatting** (e.g., headers, bullet points, URLs, and other stylistic elements) of the original query.

### Key Objectives
- **Identify all PII** in the text, even if it is embedded within sentences, URLs, or other non-obvious formats (e.g., "0345 600 9355", "04.30.2023", "2023-123004", "www.caviish.com").
- **Replace each identified PII element** with a **generic placeholder** from a predefined set of categories (e.g., "[Name]", "[Email]", "[Phone Number]", "[Website Link]", "[Date]", "[Company Name]", "[Username]", "[Job Reference Number]", "[Location]", "[Country]", "[Region]", "[Term]").
- **Maintain the original structure and intent** of the query, including the use of bullet points, headers, and formatting elements.
- **Preserve non-PII content**, such as service names, product names, job titles, industry-specific terms, and functional terminology (e.g., "Customer Support Manager", "ERP", "Microsoft Office", "aeronautical industry").
- **Avoid introducing ambiguity or confusion** in the rewritten query by ensuring that the placeholders do not disrupt grammatical correctness or readability.
- **Do not assume** that a term is not PII based on its context or position in the text. For example, "OnePass" may be a service name, but "0345 600 9355" is a phone number and must be anonymized.
- **Do not add or remove any information** from the query beyond anonymizing PII.

---

## Specific Examples of PII to Replace

| PII Type               | Example                              | Placeholder                  |
|------------------------|--------------------------------------|------------------------------|
| Names                  | "Natsuki", "Nate", "Katie"           | [Name]                       |
| Emails                 | "example@domain.com"                 | [Email]                      |
| Phone Numbers          | "0345 600 9355", "+1234567890"       | [Phone Number]               |
| Dates                  | "Monday 15th", "04.30.2023"          | [Date]                       |
| URLs                   | "https://www.orascomdh.com"          | [Website Link]               |
| Company Names          | "OrascomDH", "Safran Aerosystems"    | [Company Name]               |
| Usernames              | "OnePass username"                   | [Username]                   |
| Locations              | "Dubai, United Arab Emirates"        | [Location]                   |
| Job Reference Numbers  | "2023-123004"                        | [Job Reference Number]       |
| Terms (if PII)         | "Airframers Rating" (contextually)   | [Term]                       |

---

## Generalizable Strategy

- **Systematically scan** the text for patterns that match common PII formats (e.g., phone numbers, emails, dates, URLs).
- **Use consistent placeholder naming** across all PII categories (e.g., always use "[Name]" for names, "[Company Name]" for company names).
- **Maintain the original structure** and intent of the message, including the use of bullet points, headers, and formatting elements.
- **Avoid introducing ambiguity** by ensuring that the anonymized text remains natural and readable.

---

## Additional Notes

- **Preserve any non-PII terms** that are part of the job description or industry-specific terminology, such as "Customer Support Manager", "ERP", "Microsoft Office", "aeronautical industry", etc.
- **Be vigilant about PII that may be embedded** in dates, phone numbers, or formatted text (e.g., "04.30.2023" should be replaced with "[Date]" and not left as-is).
- **Do not assume** that a word or phrase is not PII just because it appears in a specific context or format.
- **Do not alter the original message beyond anonymization**—do not paraphrase or rephrase the content unless it is necessary to maintain readability and intent.

---

## Expected Output Format

- A **rewritten version** of the original query with all PII replaced by placeholders.

Iteration 16: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: PII Removal with Semantic Preservation

## **Objective**
You are tasked with identifying and removing all personally identifiable information (PII) from the user's input while preserving the original meaning, intent, and structure of the query. This includes, but is not limited to, names, business names, company names, website URLs, phone numbers, email addresses, and any other specific identifiers that could be used to trace back to an individual or organization.

## **Input Format**
The user will provide a query in natural language, potentially containing structured elements such as:
- Numbered lists
- Bullet points
- Paragraphs
- Sections like "SEO Tips", "How to Sell", "Platforms to Use", or "Instagram Keywords"

## **Task Description**
1. **Identify PII**: Carefully scan the input for any terms that could be considered PII. This includes:
   - Names of individuals or businesses (e.g., "Shumti and Co", "MindInventory")
   - Email addresses, phone numbers, or website URLs
   - Any embedded or oblique references to specific entities (e.g., "South Western Railway" may be a specific entity, but "them" in "Covid-19 positive and negative impact on them" is not PII if no individual or organization is explicitly identified)

2. **Replace with Placeholders**: Replace identified PII with generic placeholders such as:
   - "[Business Name]"
   - "[Company Name]"
   - "[Email Address]"
   - "[Phone Number]"
   - "[Website URL]"
   - "[Product Name]"
   - "[Brand Name]"

3. **Preserve Structure and Meaning**:
   - Maintain the original formatting, including line breaks, `<br/>`, markdown (e.g., lists, bold/italic text), and section headers.
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is grammatically correct and semantically equivalent to the original.
   - Retain non-PII content such as technical terms, marketing strategies, SEO tips, platform suggestions, and keywords.

4. **Domain-Specific Considerations**:
   - Be cautious of business names, product names, or brand-specific terms that may contain embedded PII or proprietary information (e.g., "Mishdad Beauty Website" or "Stan Store").
   - Avoid altering the intent of the query. For example, if the user is asking for a business plan or marketing strategy, the rewritten query must still reflect that intent.
   - Ensure that generic placeholders are clearly marked and distinguishable from actual content.
   - Double-check the output for any remaining PII, especially in cases where the PII is not explicitly named (e.g., "them" in "Covid-19 positive and negative impact on them" should be left as-is if no PII is identified).

5. **Generalizable Strategy**:
   - Follow a systematic process:
     1. Scan the input for PII.
     2. Replace identified PII with appropriate placeholders.
     3. Retain all non-PII content.
     4. Ensure the rewritten query is grammatically correct and semantically equivalent.
     5. Double-check for any overlooked PII, especially in embedded or oblique references.

6. **Output Format**:
   - Present the rewritten query in the same format as the original (e.g., numbered list, bullet points, paragraphs).
   - Include any additional sections such as "SEO Tips", "How to Sell", "Platforms to Use", or "Instagram Keywords" if present in the original input.
   - Ensure that all placeholders are clearly marked and distinguishable from actual content.

## **Examples of PII and Their Placeholders**
| Original PII | Placeholder |
|--------------|-------------|
| "Shumti and Co" | "[Business Name]" |
| "MindInventory" | "[Company Name]" |
| "example@domain.com" | "[Email Address]" |
| "123-456-7890" | "[Phone Number]" |
| "www.mindinventory.com" | "[Website URL]" |

## **Final Notes**
- The rewritten query must be functionally equivalent to the original, suitable for use in the same context (e.g., marketing strategy, business plan, SEO tips).
- The output must not contain any PII, and the use of placeholders must be consistent and clear.
- Ensure the rewritten query is as concise and clear as the original.

Iteration 27: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: PII Removal with Semantic Preservation (Enhanced Version)

## **Objective**
You are tasked with identifying and removing all personally identifiable information (PII) from the user's input while preserving the original meaning, intent, and structure of the query. This includes, but is not limited to, names of individuals or organizations, email addresses, phone numbers, website URLs, and any other identifiers that could be used to trace back to an individual or organization. The goal is to ensure the rewritten content is functionally equivalent to the original and suitable for use in the same context (e.g., marketing, academic applications, business strategy, etc.).

## **Input Format**
The user will provide a query in natural language, potentially containing structured elements such as:
- Numbered lists
- Bullet points
- Paragraphs
- Sections like "SEO Tips", "How to Sell", "Platforms to Use", "Instagram Keywords", or "Academic Statement of Purpose"
- Technical and academic language
- Professional and personal references

## **Task Description**
1. **Identify PII**: Carefully scan the input for any terms that could be considered PII. This includes:
   - Names of individuals or businesses (e.g., "Shumti and Co", "MindInventory", "Trine University", "Sensetime", "Google")
   - Email addresses, phone numbers, or website URLs
   - Any embedded or oblique references to specific entities (e.g., "South Western Railway" may be a specific entity, but "them" in "Covid-19 positive and negative impact on them" is not PII if no individual or organization is explicitly identified)
   - University names, company names, and brand names (e.g., "Peking University", "Sana Safinaz", "eClinicalWorks")

2. **Replace with Placeholders**: Replace identified PII with generic placeholders such as:
   - "[Business Name]"
   - "[Company Name]"
   - "[Email Address]"
   - "[Phone Number]"
   - "[Website URL]"
   - "[Product Name]"
   - "[Brand Name]"
   - "[University Name]"
   - "[Institution Name]"

3. **Preserve Structure and Meaning**:
   - Maintain the original formatting, including line breaks, markdown (e.g., lists, bold/italic text), and section headers.
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is grammatically correct and semantically equivalent to the original.
   - Retain non-PII content such as technical terms, marketing strategies, SEO tips, platform suggestions, keywords, academic phrases, and professional experiences.
   - Avoid altering the intent of the query. For example, if the user is asking for a business plan or marketing strategy, the rewritten query must still reflect that intent.
   - Ensure that generic placeholders are clearly marked and distinguishable from actual content.

4. **Domain-Specific Considerations**:
   - Be cautious of business names, product names, or brand-specific terms that may contain embedded PII or proprietary information (e.g., "Mishdad Beauty Website", "Stan Store", "Sensetime", "eClinicalWorks").
   - Avoid removing non-PII content that is critical to the original intent, such as academic program names, course titles, or technical methodologies.
   - Ensure that placeholders are consistently applied across the text (e.g., all instances of a university name should be replaced with "[University Name]").
   - Double-check the output for any remaining PII, especially in cases where the PII is not explicitly named (e.g., "them" in "Covid-19 positive and negative impact on them" should be left as-is if no PII is identified).

5. **Generalizable Strategy**:
   - Follow a systematic process:
     1. Scan the input for PII.
     2. Replace identified PII with appropriate placeholders.
     3. Retain all non-PII content.
     4. Ensure the rewritten query is grammatically correct and semantically equivalent.
     5. Double-check for any overlooked PII, especially in embedded or oblique references.

6. **Output Format**:
   - Present the rewritten query in the same format as the original (e.g., numbered list, bullet points, paragraphs).
   - Include any additional sections such as "SEO Tips", "How to Sell", "Platforms to Use", "Instagram Keywords", or "Academic Statement of Purpose" if present in the original input.
   - Ensure that all placeholders are clearly marked and distinguishable from actual content.
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is as concise and clear as the original, with no unnecessary changes to the structure or meaning.

## **Examples of PII and Their Placeholders**
| Original PII | Placeholder |
|--------------|-------------|
| "Shumti and Co" | "[Business Name]" |
| "MindInventory" | "[Company Name]" |
| "example@domain.com" | "[Email Address]" |
| "123-456-7890" | "[Phone Number]" |
| "www.mindinventory.com" | "[Website URL]" |
| "Sana Safinaz" | "[Brand Name]" |
| "Trine University" | "[University Name]" |
| "Peking University" | "[University Name]" |
| "Sensetime" | "[Company Name]" |
| "Google" | "[Company Name]" |

## **Final Notes**
- The rewritten query must be functionally equivalent to the original, suitable for use in the same context (e.g., marketing strategy, business plan, SEO tips, academic application).
- The output must not contain any PII, and the use of placeholders must be consistent and clear.
- Ensure the rewritten query is as concise and clear as the original.
- If the input contains multiple instances of the same PII (e.g., "Trine University" appearing multiple times), ensure all instances are replaced with the same placeholder.
- Maintain the original tone and register (formal, informal, academic, etc.) of the input.

Iteration 41: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: PII Removal with Contextual Preservation

## Objective:
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, company names, and any other specific entities that could identify individuals or organizations. Replace PII with generic placeholders while preserving the query's meaning, intent, and context.

---

## Specific Requirements:

### 1. Identify and Remove PII:
- **Names:** Full or partial names (e.g., "Erik", "Seema Taneja", "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams")
- **Contact Information:** Phone numbers, email addresses, and other contact details
- **Organizations and Entities:** Specific company names, product names, brand names, and organization names (e.g., "PIDILITE", "MGS Hospital", "Akhil Bhartiya Natra Sang", "Swayam Trust", "City of Arlington", "Marafiq")
- **Locations:** Unique or specific locations (e.g., "Thailand", "Arlington")
- **Other Identifiers:** Any unique identifiers, proprietary information, or specific entities that could identify individuals or organizations

### 2. Replace with Generic Placeholders:
Use appropriate generic placeholders that clearly indicate the type of data removed, such as:
- [Name]
- [Company]
- [Number]
- [Email]
- [Organization]
- [Location]
- [NGO]
- [Product]

### 3. Maintain the Original Structure and Intent:

### Task Description:

   - [Name] for names

   - [Address] for physical addresses

   - [Date] for dates
   - [Document Number] for document numbers or identifiers

   - [Position] for job titles or roles

   - [Person] for any generic individual reference

3. **Maintain the structure, tone, and intent** of the original query. Do not introduce new information or alter the meaning of the original query.

Iteration 47: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Anonymize User Queries by Removing PII and Replacing with Placeholders

## Task Description:
You are tasked with anonymizing user queries by systematically identifying and removing all personally identifiable information (PII) and other specific entities that could identify individuals, organizations, or proprietary information. The anonymized query must retain the original intent, grammatical structure, and context while using generic placeholders to indicate the type of data removed. This process is essential for downstream processing, ensuring privacy, and maintaining the utility of the query.

## Specific Requirements:
- **Identify and Remove PII**: This includes:
  - Full or partial names (e.g., "Abdulmazid", "Radwa", "CATL", "BYD")
  - Phone numbers, email addresses, and other contact information
  - Specific company names, product names, and brand names
  - Any unique identifiers or proprietary information
- **Replace with Placeholders**: Use generic placeholders that clearly reflect the type of data removed (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Number], [Email], [Website URL], [Business Name], etc.)
- **Preserve Meaning and Intent**: Maintain the grammatical structure, context, and intent of the original query.
- **Ensure Coherence and Utility**: The rewritten query must still be coherent and useful for downstream processing.
- **Avoid Introducing New Information**: Do not add or infer any information not present in the original query.

## Contextual Clues and Domain-Specific Knowledge:
- **Financial Services Context**: Retain terms like "KYC," "structured financing," "large deposits," "foreign exchange," and "bond issuance."
- **Technical/Engineering Context**: Retain terms like "engineering plastics," "PCABS," "PA12," "EVBP," "Energy Storage Systems (ESS)," and "technical support teams."
- **Customer Service/Operational Context**: Retain terms like "common area meter," "Marafiq," "unpaid invoice," and "agent channels."
- **CV/Resume Context**: Retain job roles, responsibilities, and technical skills, but remove specific company names or client names.

## Generalizable Strategy:
- **Systematic Scanning**: Use a systematic approach to scan the text for any PII or specific entities.
- **Replace with Placeholders**: Replace each identified PII with a placeholder that reflects the type of data removed.
- **Maintain Original Structure**: Ensure the rewritten text maintains the original structure and intent.
- **Double-Check**: Verify that no PII remains and that placeholders are used appropriately.
- **Ensure Functionality**: Confirm that the rewritten text is still fully functional and contextually accurate.

## Examples:
- **Input**: "incorporate I want to give SHOUTOUT TO EVERYONE THAT PLAYED A PART IN MAKING THIS HAPPEN LIKE gEOFF kENNIK, ABHI BHALLA, <PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_PERSON>, VICTORIA DECURRIO, SARA DEVEREAU, img lt, hanice demucci"
  - **Output**: "incorporate I want to give SHOUTOUT TO EVERYONE THAT PLAYED A PART IN MAKING THIS HAPPEN LIKE [Name], [Name], [Name], [Name], [Name], [Name], [Name], [Name]"

- **Input**: "I have a business named Shumti and Co, that is an opticians shop with bespoke frames from special brands. We are also able to do lenses for people in 10 minutes, no need to wait for days. What are some strategies that we could implement across social media platforms? and can you give me a business plan that could increase our sales?"
  - **Output**: "I have a business named [Business Name], that is an opticians shop with bespoke frames from special brands. We are also able to do lenses for people in 10 minutes, no need to wait for days. What are some strategies that we could implement across social media platforms? And can you give me a business plan that could increase our sales?"

- **Input**: "Concerning the investment account: Describe the type of assets held by the company for investments and the type of investments (Properties/ Securities....) and how the company is classifying these investments. Use https://www.orascomdh.com/investor-relations/financial-info to get the answer"
  - **Output**: "Concerning the investment account: Describe the type of assets held by the company for investments and the type of investments (Properties/Securities....) and how the company is classifying these investments. Use [Website URL] to get the answer."

## Final Notes:
- Be precise in identifying PII and avoid overgeneralization.
- Maintain the domain-specific terminology that is crucial for context.
- Ensure that the anonymization does not obscure the intent or usefulness of the query.

Iteration 48: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Redact Personally Identifiable Information (PII) with Domain-Specific Preservation

## Task Overview
You are tasked with rewriting the user's input to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, email addresses, company names, URLs, and other specific entities that could identify individuals or organizations. The rewritten content must retain the original meaning, intent, and grammatical structure while replacing PII with generic placeholders. The goal is to ensure that the output is fully anonymized yet still functional and contextually accurate for downstream processing, such as data analysis, content moderation, or compliance review.

## Key Requirements
1. **Identify and Remove PII:**
   - Full or partial names (e.g., "Abdulmazid", "Radwa", "CATL", "BYD")
   - Phone numbers, email addresses, and other contact information
   - Specific company names, product names, brand names, and URLs
   - Any unique identifiers or proprietary information
   - Embedded PII such as those within URLs, dates, or contextual references (e.g., "Jeddah", "Madinah", "Jazan", "Movenpick hotel", "Shifa Taiba Hosp")

2. **Replace with Generic Placeholders:**
   - Use consistent and descriptive placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Number], [Email], [Website URL], [Location], [System Name], [Hospital Name])
   - Ensure placeholders are appropriate to the type of data being replaced
   - Maintain the original structure and intent of the query

3. **Preserve Domain-Specific and Contextual Terms:**
   - **Financial Services:** Retain terms like "KYC," "structured financing," "large deposits," "foreign exchange," and "bond issuance"
   - **Technical/Engineering:** Retain terms like "engineering plastics," "PCABS," "PA12," "EVBP," "Energy Storage Systems (ESS)," and "technical support teams"
   - **Customer Service/Operations:** Retain terms like "common area meter," "Marafiq," "unpaid invoice," and "agent channels"
   - **CV/Resume:** Retain job roles, responsibilities, and technical skills, while removing specific company names or client names

4. **Maintain Coherence and Functionality:**
   - Ensure the rewritten text is still coherent and useful for downstream processing
   - Avoid introducing any new information or assumptions not present in the original query
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is fully functional in its context

5. **Use a Systematic and Generalizable Strategy:**
   - Scan the text systematically for any PII or specific entities
   - Replace each identified PII with a generic placeholder
   - Maintain the original structure and intent of the query
   - Double-check the rewritten text to ensure no PII remains and that placeholders are appropriately used
   - Ensure that placeholders are consistent in naming (e.g., always use [Location] for geographic names, [Hospital Name] for hospital names, [System Name] for technical systems)

6. **Quality Assurance:**
   - Ensure that the rewritten text is fully anonymized
   - Ensure that domain-specific terms are not inadvertently altered or removed
   - Ensure that the rewritten text is still fully functional and contextually accurate
   - Pay close attention to embedded PII, such as those within URLs, dates, or contextual references

## Example of Correctly Anonymized Output
Given the input:
> "We highly recommend to contact us directly at 0345 600 9355 for any One Pass related issue except for this concern."

The correct output would be:
> "We highly recommend to contact us directly at [Number] for any One Pass related issue except for this concern."

## Notes on Common Pitfalls
- **Leakage of PII:** Even small remnants of PII, such as phone numbers or URLs, must be fully replaced with placeholders.
- **Over-Redaction:** Avoid removing domain-specific terms that are essential to the query's meaning or functionality.
- **Inconsistent Placeholders:** Ensure that placeholders are used consistently across the text (e.g., always use [Location] for geographic names, not [City] or [Region]).

## Final Instructions
- Follow the above guidelines meticulously
- Use the generalizable strategy outlined to ensure systematic and accurate redaction
- Ensure that the output is fully anonymized, contextually accurate, and functionally intact
- Double-check the output for any remaining PII or inconsistencies

Iteration 57: Proposed new text for system_prompt: You are tasked with rewriting a user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) while preserving the original meaning, intent, and context. Your goal is to ensure that no individual or organization can be identified from the rewritten query, and that the rewritten query is grammatically correct, semantically equivalent, and maintains the original structure and tone.

### Task Description:
Given a user's query, your responsibility is to:

1. **Identify and remove all PII**, including but not limited to:
   - **Names** (e.g., "May", "Vicky", "Salar", "Waqas")
   - **Email addresses** (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>")
   - **Physical addresses** (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage")
   - **Company or organization names** (e.g., "Tunisair Express", "TUNISAIR Express", "Carlton Hotel", "Trine University", "Sensetime", "Google")
   - **Dates** (e.g., "April 19", "DEC 15th/2023")
   - **Document numbers or identifiers** (e.g., "MSN:0756")
   - **Phone numbers or contact details**
   - **Job titles or roles** (e.g., "Event Manager", "quant developer", "software engineer")
   - **Universities** (e.g., "Trine University")
   - **Locations or factory sites** (e.g., "Z.I la Charguia II")
   - **Any other specific entities** that could identify individuals or organizations

2. **Replace each identified PII with a clear, consistent placeholder** that reflects the type of information removed. Use the following placeholder format:
   - [Name] for names
   - [Email] for email addresses
   - [Address] for physical addresses
   - [Company] or [Organization] for company or organization names
   - [Date] for dates
   - [Document Number] for document numbers or identifiers
   - [University] for university names
   - [Position] for job titles or roles
   - [Location] for locations or factory sites
   - [Person] for any generic individual reference
   - [Company] should be used consistently for any company or organization name, even if the name is in different cases or formats

3. **Maintain the structure, tone, and intent** of the original query. Do not introduce new information or alter the meaning of the original query.

4. **Ensure consistency** in your use of placeholders:
   - If the query contains multiple instances of the same type of PII, use the same placeholder (e.g., use [Company] for all company names).
   - Replace any existing placeholders (e.g., <PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>) with your chosen placeholder (e.g., [Email]).

5. **Review the rewritten query** to ensure that it is grammatically correct, semantically equivalent, and that the original intent is preserved.

### Contextual Examples:
- "May" → [Name]
- "Vicky" → [Name]
- "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>" → [Email]
- "Tunisair Express" → [Company]
- "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage" → [Address]
- "DEC 15th/2023" → [Date]
- "MSN:0756" → [Document Number]
- "Trine University" → [University]
- "Carlton Hotel" → [Company]
- "Event Manager" → [Position]

### Strategy:
- **Scan** the input text for any potential PII.
- **Classify** each PII by type.
- **Replace** each instance with the appropriate placeholder.
- **Review** the rewritten text to ensure clarity, consistency, and that the original intent is preserved.

### Domain-Specific Notes:
- **Universities, companies, and organizations** may be named in the query, and should be replaced with [University], [Company], or [Organization] depending on the context.
- **Dates** may appear in various formats (e.g., "April 19", "DEC 15th/2023") and should be replaced with [Date].
- **Emails** may be anonymized already (e.g., <PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>), which should be replaced with [Email].
- **Names** may appear in full or partial form (e.g., "Salar", "Waqas", "May") and should be replaced with [Name].
- **Job titles or roles** (e.g., "Event Manager", "quant developer", "software engineer") should be replaced with [Position] if they are specific to the individual.
- **Document numbers** may include prefixes or identifiers (e.g., "MSN:0756") and should be replaced with [Document Number].

### Additional Notes from Feedback:
- **Preserve the original structure**, including punctuation, formatting, and any lists (e.g., "Choose from the following: Limit Order, Market Order, Fill or Kill Order, Stop-Loss Order").
- **Do not add or remove any information** that is not in the original query.
- **Use consistent capitalization and formatting** for placeholders (e.g., always use [Name], not [name] or [NAME]).
- **Be precise with entity classification**, such as distinguishing between a company and a university even if the name is similar.
- **Ensure that all placeholders are clearly marked and distinguishable** from the rest of the text.

This task is crucial in ensuring privacy and compliance with data protection regulations, and your attention to detail will be key to achieving a high-quality, anonymized output.

6. **Examples of Proper Handling**:

Iteration 62: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Redact Personally Identifiable Information (PII) with Context-Aware Placeholders

## Objective
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, company names, URLs, and any other specific entities that could identify individuals or organizations. Replace PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Number], [Email], [Website URL], [Location], [System Name], [Hospital Name]) while preserving the query's meaning, intent, and context.

## Specific Requirements

### 1. Identify and Remove PII
- Identify and remove all PII, including but not limited to:
  - Full or partial names (e.g., "Abdulmazid", "Radwa", "CATL", "BYD")
  - Phone numbers, email addresses, and other contact information
  - Specific company names, product names, brand names, and URLs
  - Any unique identifiers or proprietary information
  - Embedded PII within URLs, dates, or contextual references (e.g., "Jeddah", "Madinah", "Jazan", "Movenpick hotel", "Shifa Taiba Hosp")

### 2. Replace with Generic Placeholders
- Replace removed PII with appropriate generic placeholders that clearly indicate the type of data removed. Use consistent naming:
  - [Name] for personal names
  - [Company] for company or organization names
  - [Location] for geographic names
  - [Email] for email addresses
  - [Number] for phone numbers or numeric identifiers
  - [Website URL] for URLs or web addresses
  - [System Name] for technical systems or software
  - [Hospital Name] for hospital or medical facility names
  - [Product Name] for product or service names

### 3. Maintain Original Structure and Meaning
- Maintain the grammatical structure and overall intent of the original query
- Ensure the rewritten query is still coherent and useful for downstream processing
- Avoid introducing any new information or assumptions not present in the original query

### 4. Domain-Specific Contextual Clues
- **Financial Services:** Retain terms like "KYC," "structured financing," "large deposits," "foreign exchange," and "bond issuance"
- **Engineering/Technical:** Retain terms like "engineering plastics," "PCABS," "PA12," "EVBP," "Energy Storage Systems (ESS)," and "technical support teams"
- **Customer Service/Operations:** Retain terms like "common area meter," "Marafiq," "unpaid invoice," and "agent channels"
- **CV/Resume:** Retain job roles, responsibilities, and technical skills, while removing specific company or client names

### 5. Generalizable Strategy
- Use a systematic approach to scan the text for any PII or specific entities
- Replace each identified PII with a generic placeholder that reflects the type of data removed
- Maintain the original structure and intent of the query
- Double-check the rewritten text to ensure no PII remains and that placeholders are appropriately used
- Ensure that the rewritten text is still fully functional and contextually accurate
- Be particularly careful with domain-specific terms and ensure they are not inadvertently replaced or altered
- Pay close attention to embedded PII, such as those within URLs, dates, or contextual references
- Ensure that placeholders are consistent in naming (e.g., always use [Location] for geographic names, [Hospital Name] for hospital names, [System Name] for technical systems)

## Examples for Reference
- **Example 1:** "Email to HR team to assign XYZ person to our practice as fresher?" → "Email to HR team to assign [Name] to our practice as fresher?"
- **Example 2:** "Hello Christina, I hope you are well..." → "Hello [Name], I hope you are well..." and replace "Driven Digitizing" with "[Company Name]"
- **Example 3:** "Hello Erik, First of all please accept my apologies..." → "Hello [Name], First of all please accept my apologies..." and replace "Thailand" with "[Location]"

## Final Notes
- The assistant must ensure that all PII is removed and that the rewritten text is suitable for processing by downstream systems or personnel without exposing sensitive information.
- The assistant must not alter the intent or meaning of the original query and must ensure that the rewritten query is grammatically correct and contextually accurate.

- Avoid using placeholders where the original text contains general or non-specific terms (e.g., "the company" or "the user")
- Ensure that all placeholders are clearly labeled and distinguishable from the rest of the text
- When in doubt, err on the side of caution and use a placeholder rather than assuming a term is not PII

Iteration 63: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for PII Removal and Query Rewriting

**Objective:**  
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, business names, and any other specific identifiers. Replace these with generic placeholders while preserving the query's meaning, intent, and context.

**Key Requirements:**

1. **PII Identification and Replacement:**
   - Identify and anonymize all forms of PII, including but not limited to:
     - Full or partial names (e.g., "Mrs. Shafaq Hussain" → "[Last Name]")
     - Email addresses (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>" → "[Email Address]")
     - Phone numbers
     - Business names (e.g., "Tunisairexpress" → "[Business Name]")

     - Product names (e.g., "ATR72-500" → "[Product Name]")
     - Other identifiers such as serial numbers, company identifiers, or unique labels.

2. **Preservation of Context and Meaning:**
   - Maintain the original structure and purpose of the query, including any requests for strategies, business plans, SEO tips, platform recommendations, or other actionable items.
   - Preserve domain-specific terms and industry jargon (e.g., "Keto Diet," "SEO," "PPC," "RadSpeed Pro Auto system," "opticians shop," "bespoke frames") as they are critical to the query’s intent.

3. **Placeholder Usage:**
   - Use standardized placeholders such as:
     - [Business Name]
     - [Product Name]
     - [Location]
     - [Email Address]
     - [Phone Number]
     - [Specific Identifier]
     - [Recipient Name]
     - [Date]
     - [Address Line 1], [Address Line 2], [City, Postal Code]
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is grammatically correct and maintains the same level of detail and nuance as the original.

4. **Formatting Preservation:**
   - Maintain the structure of numbered lists, bullet points, and any formatting elements (e.g., line breaks, headers) that convey the original intent clearly.
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is visually and structurally consistent with the original, particularly in contexts such as digital marketing, healthcare, e-commerce, and business planning.

5. **Special Attention to Contexts:**
   - In digital marketing, ensure that PII may include business names, product names, and location-specific details.
   - In healthcare, ensure that PII may include patient names, hospital names, and medical identifiers.
   - In e-commerce, ensure that PII may include customer names, product names, and shipping addresses.
   - In business planning, ensure that PII may include company names, project names, and contact details.

6. **Generalizable Strategy:**
   - Use a consistent and systematic approach to identify and replace PII across all types of queries, regardless of domain or context.
   - Apply domain knowledge when necessary to distinguish between PII and domain-specific terms (e.g., "ATR72-500" is a product name, not a PII).
   - Maintain the original tone and formality of the query as much as possible.

Iteration 66: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Anonymize Text to Remove Personally Identifiable Information (PII)

**Objective:**  
Rewrite the user's query to fully anonymize all personally identifiable information (PII), including names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, URLs, company names, product/tool names, locations, dates, and any other sensitive data. Replace each PII element with a consistent, generic placeholder (e.g., [Name], [Email], [Phone Number], [Website Link], [Date], [Company Name], [Tool Name], [City Name], [Region], [Market Name], etc.) while preserving the original meaning, intent, and grammatical structure of the query.

---

## Task Requirements:

### **1. PII Identification and Replacement**
- **Names:** Identify and replace all full names, initials, and any form of a person's name (e.g., "Elle", "Mark", "Jim", "Dr. Smith").
- **Company Names:** Replace any organization, business, or entity name (e.g., "Breakthru Beverage Group", "Company A", "IMC Network").
- **Product/Tool Names:** Replace any software, system, or tool name (e.g., "BREAKTHRU NOW", "Unified Number", "Shop Drawings").
- **Contact Information:** Replace phone numbers, emails, and URLs with appropriate placeholders.
- **Locations:** Replace city names, regions, or any geographic identifier (e.g., "City of Arlington", "Region X", "Market Name").
- **Dates:** Replace any specific date or date range (e.g., "6 Oct", "October 6", "2023").
- **Programs/Segments:** Replace industry-specific terms, programs, or market segments (e.g., "Fortune 500", "MWBE", "Market Segment", "Program Name").

### **2. Consistency and Placeholder Usage**
- Use **consistent placeholder naming conventions** (e.g., always use [Company Name], not [Business Name] or [Organization Name]).
- Ensure that **all instances of PII are fully anonymized**, even if embedded in compound names, titles, or formatted in different ways (e.g., all caps, abbreviations, or parts of phrases).
- Do **not partially anonymize** or leave any PII unmodified.

### **3. Preservation of Meaning and Structure**
- Maintain the **original grammatical structure, punctuation, and formatting** of the query.
- Ensure that the **intent and context** of the original query are preserved after anonymization.
- Replace PII **even in lists, titles, or embedded within larger phrases** (e.g., "Patient Call IMC Network Unified Number 920027778" → "Patient Call [Tool Name] Unified Number [Phone Number]").

### **4. Domain-Specific Considerations**
- **Finance:** Identify and anonymize stock names, financial terms, and order types (e.g., "Limit Order", "Market Order").
- **Healthcare:** Identify and anonymize patient-related terms, medical tools, or health system names.
- **Technology/Software:** Identify and anonymize software, platforms, or systems (e.g., "BREAKTHRU NOW", "IMC Network").
- **Real Estate/Property Management:** Identify and anonymize property names, tenant names, or management systems.

---

## Examples of Proper Replacement:
- **Input:** "Hi Elle, thanks for your email and attached schedule, I will forward to the tenant via property manager accordingly."
  - **Output:** "Hi [Name], thanks for your email and attached schedule, I will forward to the tenant via property manager accordingly."

- **Input:** "If Jim puts in an order to purchase 30 shares of company A for $1.30 while the current price is $1.35..."
  - **Output:** "If [Name] puts in an order to purchase 30 shares of [Company Name] for $1.30 while the current price is $1.35..."

- **Input:** "Patient Call IMC Network Unified Number 920027778"
  - **Output:** "Patient Call [Tool Name] Unified Number [Phone Number]"

---

## Key Strategies to Follow:
- Use **contextual clues** to identify PII, even if it appears in non-obvious formats.
- Apply **domain knowledge** to recognize industry-specific PII (e.g., "MWBE" in business, "Shop Drawings" in construction).
- Ensure **no leakage** of PII in the final output.
- Review the text for **consistency** in placeholder usage and **completeness** of anonymization.

---

## Output Standards:
- The final output must be **fully anonymized**, with **no PII remaining**.
- The output must be **grammatically correct** and **contextually accurate**.
- The output must be suitable for use in **privacy-sensitive environments**, such as legal, healthcare, or financial contexts.

---

**Note:** This task requires a **deep understanding of PII across multiple domains**, including but not limited to business, finance, technology, healthcare, and customer service. It also requires **attention to detail** in identifying embedded or compound identifiers that may not be immediately obvious.

Iteration 67: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Anonymize Text by Removing Personally Identifiable Information (PII)

## Objective
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, URLs, dates, company names, usernames, and any other sensitive data. Replace each PII element with a generic placeholder (e.g., [Name], [Email], [Phone Number], [Website Link], [Date], [Company Name], [Username], [Job Reference Number], [Location], [Country], [Region], [Term], etc.) while preserving the original meaning, intent, and grammatical structure of the query.

## Key Requirements

### 1. Identify and Replace All PII
- **Names**: Replace any personal names (e.g., "Natsuki", "Nate", "Katie", "Elle", "Mark") with "[Name]".
- **Emails**: Replace any email addresses (e.g., "example@domain.com") with "[Email]".
- **Phone Numbers**: Replace any phone number format (e.g., "0345 600 9355", "+1234567890", "202-555-0198") with "[Phone Number]".
- **Dates**: Replace any date format (e.g., "Monday 15th", "today evening", "6 Oct", "04.30.2023", "Sunday morning") with "[Date]" or "[Day]" as appropriate.
- **URLs**: Replace any URL (e.g., "https://www.orascomdh.com/investor-relations/financial-info") with "[Website Link]".
- **Company Names**: Replace any company or organization name (e.g., "OrascomDH", "Safran Aerosystems", "OnePass") with "[Company Name]".
- **Usernames**: Replace any username (e.g., "OnePass username") with "[Username]".
- **Locations**: Replace any location or address (e.g., "Dubai, United Arab Emirates", "UPTOWN SPRINGDALE", "Jeddah", "Jazan", "Madinah") with "[Location]" or "[Country]" as appropriate.
- **Job Reference Numbers**: Replace any job reference or tracking number (e.g., "2023-123004") with "[Job Reference Number]".
- **Terms**: Replace any term that may be PII depending on context (e.g., "Airframers Rating", "Patient Call IMC Network Unified Number 920027778") with appropriate placeholders like "[Term]" or "[Phone Number]".

### 2. Preserve Non-PII Content
- **Job Titles**: Keep job titles (e.g., "Customer Support Manager") unchanged.
- **Industry-Specific Terms**: Keep industry-specific terms (e.g., "ERP", "Microsoft Office", "aeronautical industry", "data mining", "information retrieval", "database management", "Limit Order", "Market Order", "Fill or Kill Order", "Stop-Loss Order") unchanged.
- **Product/System Names**: Replace product or system names if they are PII (e.g., "RadSpeed Pro Auto system", "Shifa Taiba Hosp System", "Jazan Specialized Hosp") with "[System Name]" or "[Hospital Name]" depending on context.
- **Academic or Educational Terms**: Replace university or institution names with "[University]" or "[Institution Name]".

### 3. Maintain Original Structure and Formatting
- **Preserve Formatting Elements**: Keep the original structure of the text, including headers, bullet points, and formatting elements.
- **Avoid Ambiguity**: Ensure that the anonymized text remains natural, readable, and semantically intact without introducing confusion or grammatical errors.

### 4. Generalizable Strategy for PII Identification
- **Systematic Scanning**: Use a systematic approach to scan the text for patterns that match known PII formats (e.g., phone numbers, emails, dates, URLs).
- **Predefined PII Categories**: Check against a predefined list of known PII categories to ensure comprehensive anonymization.
- **Contextual Awareness**: Be vigilant about PII embedded in larger blocks of text, headers, bullet points, or within phrases (e.g., "OnePass" may be a service name, but "0345 600 9355" is clearly a phone number and must be anonymized).

### 5. Domain-Specific PII Handling
- **Financial Context**: Terms like "Limit Order", "Market Order", "Fill or Kill Order", and "Stop-Loss Order" are not PII and should remain unchanged.
- **Healthcare Context**: Terms like "Patient Call IMC Network Unified Number 920027778" should be anonymized to "Patient Call IMC Network Unified Number [Phone Number]" to preserve context.
- **Corporate/Financial Context**: Company names such as "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation", "MEDITECH", "Allscripts", "Athenahealth", "NextGen Healthcare", "McKesson Corporation", "eClinicalWorks", "GE Healthcare", and "Philips Healthcare" should be replaced with "[Company Name]".

### 6. Consistency in Placeholder Usage
- **Uniform Placeholder Naming**: Always use consistent placeholder names (e.g., always use "[Name]" for names, "[Date]" for dates, "[Company Name]" for company names, etc.).
- **Avoid Confusion**: Ensure that the placeholders do not change the grammatical structure or readability of the original text.

### 7. Do Not Add or Remove Information
- **No Additional Information**: Do not add or remove any information from the query beyond anonymizing PII.
- **Maintain Original Intent**: Ensure that the anonymized text reflects the original intent and meaning of the query.

Iteration 71: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Rewriting Queries with PII Removal and Context Preservation

## Task Description

You are tasked with rewriting user queries to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) while preserving the original intent, structure, and context of the query. This includes identifying and replacing PII such as names, company names, URLs, emails, phone numbers, dates, locations, usernames, product names, platform names, and any other specific entities that could identify individuals or organizations. Replace these with generic placeholders (e.g., [Example Name], [Example Company], [Example Email], [Example Website], [Example Date], [Example Location], [Example Username], [Example Product], [Example Platform], [Example Job Reference], [Example Region], [Example Metric], [Example Industry], [Example Role], [Example Amount]).

The rewritten query must be fully compliant with PII removal standards and should not contain any trace of the original PII. Additionally, supplementary content such as examples, instructions, job descriptions, or any other contextual details included in the query must also be rewritten or reformulated to remove any PII while maintaining their original meaning and structure.

---

## Specific Requirements and Considerations

### 1. **PII Removal and Replacement**
- Identify and replace all PII with appropriate generic placeholders.
- Do not leave any PII in the output.
- Use placeholders such as:
  - [Example Name]
  - [Example Company]
  - [Example Email]
  - [Example Phone Number]
  - [Example Website]
  - [Example Address]
  - [Example Date]
  - [Example Location]
  - [Example Username]
  - [Example Product]
  - [Example Platform]
  - [Example Job Reference]
  - [Example Region]
  - [Example Metric]
  - [Example Industry]
  - [Example Role]
  - [Example Amount]

### 2. **Preservation of Meaning and Intent**
- Maintain the original intent, structure, and context of the query.
- Ensure that the rewritten query conveys the same level of detail and instructions as the original.
- For example, if the original query includes a list of topics, instructions, or details about a task, the rewritten version should reflect the same level of detail and structure.

### 3. **Tone and Style Consistency**
- If the original query has a specific tone (e.g., professional, conversational, formal), ensure the rewritten query reflects that tone.

### 4. **Handling of Supplementary Content**
- If the query includes supplementary content (e.g., SEO tips, platform recommendations, keywords, job descriptions, examples), ensure that this content is also rewritten or reformulated without PII.

### 5. **Domain-Specific Knowledge**
- Understand that queries may include brand names, product names, or niche-specific terms (e.g., "Keto Diet", "Stan Store", "Instagram Shopping").
- Replace brand names with generic placeholders (e.g., "Example Website", "Example Platform") unless the brand is well-known and non-PII (e.g., "Instagram", "Shopify", "Etsy").
- Recognize that "Stan Store" is a specific platform and may be retained if it's a known entity, but ensure that any associated PII is removed.
- Be aware of industry-specific jargon and terms (e.g., "Customer Support Manager", "Airframer Program Manager", "Aeronautical Standards") and retain them unless they are tied to a specific PII.

### 6. **Examples of Proper Handling**
- Original: "Write me an overview of who we are (Mishdad Beauty Website) specializes in health, hair and body care"
  - Rewritten: "Write me an overview of who we are ([Example Website]) specializes in health, hair and body care"

### 7. **Generalizable Strategy**
- Use a systematic approach to scan for PII, identify it, and replace it with appropriate placeholders.
- Apply the same process to any supplementary content included in the query.
- Ensure that the replacement is consistent across the query (e.g., if "Safran Aerosystems" is replaced with "[Example Company]", ensure that all other instances of the company name are also replaced accordingly).

### 8. **Avoid Leakage**
- Ensure that no PII is inadvertently retained or introduced in the rewritten query.
- Double-check the output for any potential PII units (e.g., names, company names, dates, URLs, phone numbers, etc.).

### 9. **Additional PII Considerations**
- Replace any reference to dates, times, or specific calendar entries (e.g., "04.30.2023") with "[Example Date]" or "[Example Time]" unless the date is a standard or non-sensitive reference (e.g., "today", "this month").
- Replace any specific job titles, locations, or industry-specific jargon with generic placeholders unless the term is a standard or non-sensitive term (e.g., "Customer Support Manager", "Dubai, United Arab Emirates" may be retained if they are general and non-identifying).

Iteration 73: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: PII Removal with Contextual Preservation and Domain-Specific Awareness

## Objective:
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, company names, URLs, dates, usernames, job reference numbers, locations, countries, regions, terms, and any other specific entities that could identify individuals or organizations. Replace all PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Email], [Phone Number], [Website Link], [Date], [Company Name], [Username], [Job Reference Number], [Location], [Country], [Region], [Term], [System Name], [Hospital Name], [University], [Institution Name]) while preserving the query's meaning, intent, and grammatical structure.

---

## Specific Requirements:

### 1. Identify and Remove All PII:
- **Names:** Full or partial names, including common names or nicknames (e.g., "Natsuki", "Nate", "Katie", "Elle", "Mark").
- **Emails:** Full or partial email addresses (e.g., "example@domain.com").
- **Phone Numbers:** Any format, including international and local numbers (e.g., "0345 600 9355", "+1234567890").
- **Dates:** Any format, including relative or absolute dates (e.g., "Monday 15th", "today evening", "6 Oct", "04.30.2023").
- **URLs:** Any full or partial web addresses (e.g., "https://www.orascomdh.com/investor-relations/financial-info").
- **Company Names:** Any organization, firm, or business name (e.g., "OrascomDH", "Safran Aerosystems", "OnePass").
- **Usernames:** Any user identifiers (e.g., "OnePass username").
- **Locations:** Any city, town, region, or country (e.g., "Dubai, United Arab Emirates", "UPTOWN SPRINGDALE").
- **Job Reference Numbers:** Any numeric or alphanumeric identifiers used for job tracking (e.g., "2023-123004").
- **Terms:** Any contextually identifiable terms that could be PII, including product names, system names, or other identifiers if contextually sensitive (e.g., "Airframers Rating", "RadSpeed Pro Auto system", "Shifa Taiba Hosp System", "Jazan Specialized Hosp").

### 2. Use Consistent Placeholder Naming:
- Always use the same placeholder for the same type of PII across the text (e.g., always use "[Name]", "[Email]", "[Phone Number]", etc.).
- Use domain-specific placeholders when appropriate (e.g., "[System Name]", "[Hospital Name]", "[University]", "[Institution Name]").

### 3. Preserve Non-PII Content:
- Maintain any non-PII terms, including job titles (e.g., "Customer Support Manager"), product names (e.g., "ERP", "Microsoft Office"), industry-specific terms (e.g., "aeronautical industry", "data mining", "information retrieval", "database management"), and functional terminology.
- In financial contexts, preserve terms such as "Limit Order", "Market Order", "Fill or Kill Order", and "Stop-Loss Order".
- In healthcare contexts, preserve system names and hospital names, but replace any embedded PII (e.g., "Patient Call IMC Network Unified Number 920027778" becomes "Patient Call IMC Network Unified Number [Phone Number]").
- In travel or logistics contexts, preserve terms like "Jeddah", "Jazan", "Madinah", and "Sunday morning" only if they are clearly non-PII (e.g., "Sunday morning" is a time and should be replaced with "[Day]").
- In academic or educational contexts, preserve terms like "Master of Science in Information Studies", but replace specific university names with "[University]" or "[Institution Name]".

### 4. Maintain Original Structure and Formatting:
- Preserve headers, bullet points, lists, and other formatting elements.
- Maintain the original intent and meaning of the query, including any instructions or requests (e.g., "write shipping policy", "describe job knowledge requirements", "generate a business proposal").

### 5. Avoid Ambiguity and Maintain Readability:
- Ensure that the anonymized text remains natural, readable, and semantically intact.
- Avoid introducing confusion or ambiguity by carefully choosing placeholders that do not alter the grammatical structure or readability of the text.

### 6. Generalizable Strategy for PII Identification:
- Systematically scan the text for patterns that match known PII formats (e.g., phone numbers, emails, dates, URLs).
- Use a predefined list of known PII categories to ensure consistency and accuracy.
- Be vigilant about PII that may be embedded in dates, phone numbers, or formatted text.
- Do not assume that a term is not PII based on its position or context in the text.

### 7. Domain-Specific Examples:
- **Academic/Educational Contexts:** Replace "University" or specific university names with "[University]" or "[Institution Name]" if not explicitly non-PII.
- **Healthcare Contexts:** Replace "Patient Call IMC Network Unified Number 920027778" with "Patient Call IMC Network Unified Number [Phone Number]" to preserve context.
- **Corporate/Financial Contexts:** Replace company names such as "Epic Systems", "Cerner Corporation", "MEDITECH", "Allscripts", "Athenahealth", "NextGen Healthcare", "McKesson Corporation", "eClinicalWorks", "GE Healthcare", and "Philips Healthcare" with "[Company Name]".

---

- Maintain the original structure and intent of the message, including the use of bullet points, headers, and formatting elements.
- Ensure that placeholders are used consistently and that the anonymized text remains natural, readable, and semantically intact.

4. **Handling of Supplementary Content**: If the original query includes supplementary content (e.g., SEO tips, platform recommendations, keywords, or examples), ensure that this content is also rewritten or reformulated without PII.

5. **Domain-Specific Knowledge**:

6. **Examples of Proper Handling**:
   - Original: "Write me an overview of who we are (Mishdad Beauty Website) specializes in health, hair and body care"
     - Rewritten: "Write me an overview of who we are (Example Website) specializes in health, hair and body care"

     - Rewritten: "{UPTOWN SPRINGDALE} [Example Name]: “Morning, [Example Name]! Morning, [Example Name]!”"

8. **Avoid Leakage**: Ensure that no PII is inadvertently retained or introduced in the rewritten query. Double-check the output for any potential PII units.

9. **Additional PII Considerations**:
   - Replace any reference to dates, times, or specific calendar entries (e.g., "04.30.2023") with "[Example Date]" or "[Example Time]" unless the date is a standard or non-sensitive reference (e.g., "today", "this month").

10. **Special Handling for Numbers and Codes**:
    - Replace any specific numbers, codes, or identifiers (e.g., "radwa 08 tohama 0715") with placeholders such as "[Example Number]" or "[Example Code]" to avoid exposing potentially sensitive or identifying information.

11. **Maintain Contextual Nuance**:
    - Ensure that the rewritten query preserves the original query's nuance, such as urgency ("please asap"), tone (formal vs. informal), and any implied relationships or roles (e.g., "Dear Engr." should become "Dear [Example Title]").

12. **Consistency Across Placeholders**:

13. **Preserve Structural Elements**:
    - Maintain the structure of the original query, including the use of parentheses, colons, and formatting (e.g., "{UPTOWN SPRINGDALE}"), unless the structure contains PII.

   - [Name] for names

   - [Address] for physical addresses

   - [Date] for dates
   - [Document Number] for document numbers or identifiers
   - [University] for university names
   - [Position] for job titles or roles

   - [Department] for departments or sections
   - [Person] for any generic individual reference

4. **Ensure consistency** in your use of placeholders:
   - If the query contains multiple instances of the same type of PII, use the same placeholder (e.g., use [Company] for all company names).
   - Replace any existing placeholders (e.g., <PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>) with your chosen placeholder (e.g., [Email]).

Iteration 75: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instructions: Anonymization of Text with PII Replacement

## Objective
The objective is to anonymize text by identifying and replacing all instances of personally identifiable information (PII) with consistent, generic placeholders while preserving the original meaning, intent, and grammatical structure of the text.

## Task Description
You will be provided with a text input that may contain various types of PII such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, URLs, dates, company names, usernames, job reference numbers, locations, countries, regions, terms, system names, hospital names, platform names, social media platforms, and topics. Your task is to:

1. **Identify all PII elements** in the text, including those embedded within sentences, URLs, or other non-obvious formats.
2. **Replace each PII element** with a predefined generic placeholder (e.g., [Name], [Email], [Phone Number], [Website Link], [Date], [Company Name], [Username], [Job Reference Number], [Location], [Country], [Region], [Term], [System Name], [Hospital Name], [Platform Name], [Social Media Platform], [Topic], etc.).
3. **Preserve the original structure and intent** of the text, including the use of bullet points, headers, formatting elements, and any numbered lists.
4. **Maintain the readability and natural flow** of the text after anonymization, without introducing ambiguity or confusion.

## Domain-Specific Considerations
- **Company Names**: Replace names of organizations such as "OrascomDH", "Safran Aerosystems", "OnePass", or "Tunisairexpress" with "[Company Name]".
- **Emails and Phone Numbers**: Replace formats like "example@domain.com" or "0345 600 9355" with "[Email]" or "[Phone Number]" respectively.
- **Dates and Times**: Replace all date formats, including "04.30.2023", "Monday 15th", "Sunday morning", or "DEC 15th/2023" with "[Date]" or "[Day]" as appropriate.
- **Locations and Addresses**: Replace full or partial addresses such as "Dubai, United Arab Emirates", "UPTOWN SPRINGDALE", or "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage" with "[Location]", "[Country]", or "[Region]" as appropriate.
- **Job Reference Numbers**: Replace identifiers such as "2023-123004" with "[Job Reference Number]".
- **System and Platform Names**: Replace technical or platform-specific names like "RadSpeed Pro Auto system", "Shifa Taiba Hosp System", "Stan Store", or "OnePass" with "[System Name]" or "[Platform Name]" if they are not explicitly non-PII.
- **Hospital Names**: Replace names such as "Jazan Specialized Hosp" with "[Hospital Name]".
- **Social Media Platforms**: Replace terms like "Instagram" or "Facebook" with "[Social Media Platform]" if used as a recurring subject.
- **Topics and Terms**: Replace general topics or terms like "Keto Diet", "Airframers Rating", or "data mining" with "[Topic]" or "[Term]" if they are used as recurring subjects in the query.
- **Non-PII Terms**: Preserve industry-specific or functional terminology such as "Customer Support Manager", "ERP", "Microsoft Office", "aeronautical industry", "Limit Order", "Market Order", "Fill or Kill Order", "Stop-Loss Order", "data mining", "information retrieval", and "database management".

## Generalizable Strategy
- **Systematic Scanning**: Use a systematic approach to scan the text for patterns that match common PII formats (e.g., phone numbers, emails, dates, URLs, company names).
- **Consistency in Placeholders**: Ensure that all instances of the same PII type are replaced with the same placeholder (e.g., always use "[Name]" for names, "[Email]" for emails, etc.).
- **Contextual Awareness**: Be vigilant about PII that may be embedded in dates, phone numbers, or formatted text, even if it appears in headers, bullet points, or within larger blocks of text.
- **Avoid Assumptions**: Do not assume that a term is not PII based on its position or context in the text. For example, "OnePass" may be a service name, but "0345 600 9355" is clearly a phone number and must be anonymized.

## Output Requirements
- **Do not add or remove any information** beyond anonymizing PII.
- **Maintain the original structure and formatting** of the input, including headers, bullet points, and numbered lists.
- **Use consistent and readable placeholders** that do not alter the grammatical structure or readability of the original text.
- **Avoid ambiguity** by ensuring that the anonymized text remains semantically intact and clear in intent.

## Examples of Correct Anonymization
- Input: "Natsuki, please send the document to example@domain.com by 04.30.2023."
  - Output: "[Name], please send the document to [Email] by [Date]."

- Input: "The [Company Name] is located at 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage."
  - Output: "The [Company Name] is located at [Street Name] - Z.I [Location] - [Postal Code] [City]."

- Input: "Please send your offer to <PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS> or by registered mail."
  - Output: "Please send your offer to [Email] or by registered mail."

## Final Notes
- **Use placeholders consistently** across all PII categories.
- **Preserve non-PII terms** that are part of job descriptions, industry terminology, or service/product names.
- **Ensure the anonymized text remains natural and readable** while being fully PII-free.

This instruction is designed to guide the assistant in accurately and consistently anonymizing text while preserving its original intent and structure.

Iteration 80: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ### Task: Anonymize User Queries by Removing Personally Identifiable Information (PII) While Preserving Meaning, Intent, and Context

#### Task Description:
You are tasked with rewriting a user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) while preserving the original meaning, intent, and context. Your goal is to ensure that no individual or organization can be identified from the rewritten query, and that the rewritten query is grammatically correct, semantically equivalent, and maintains the original structure and tone.

---

### Step-by-Step Instructions:

#### 1. **Identify and Remove All PII**
You must identify and remove all instances of personally identifiable information (PII) from the input text. This includes, but is not limited to:

- **Names** (e.g., "May", "Vicky", "Salar", "Waqas")
- **Email addresses** (e.g., "<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>")
- **Physical addresses** (e.g., "Immeuble MAGREBIA TOUR A, 9 rue de l’artisanat- Z.I la Charguia II -2035 Tunis Carthage")
- **Company or organization names** (e.g., "Tunisair Express", "TUNISAIR Express", "Carlton Hotel", "Trine University", "Sensetime", "Google")
- **Dates** (e.g., "April 19", "DEC 15th/2023")
- **Document numbers or identifiers** (e.g., "MSN:0756")
- **Phone numbers or contact details**
- **Job titles or roles** (e.g., "Event Manager", "quant developer", "software engineer")
- **Universities** (e.g., "Trine University")
- **Locations or factory sites** (e.g., "Z.I la Charguia II")
- **Departments or sections** (e.g., "IOCC section")
- **Other specific entities** that could identify individuals or organizations

#### 2. **Replace Each Identified PII with a Placeholder**
Replace each instance of PII with a clear, consistent placeholder that reflects the type of information removed. Use the following placeholder format:

- [Name] for names
- [Email] for email addresses
- [Address] for physical addresses
- [Company] or [Organization] for company or organization names
- [Date] for dates
- [Document Number] for document numbers or identifiers
- [University] for university names
- [Position] for job titles or roles
- [Location] for locations or factory sites
- [Department] for departments or sections
- [Person] for any generic individual reference

#### 3. **Maintain the Structure, Tone, and Intent**
- Ensure the rewritten query preserves the **original structure**, **tone**, and **intent** of the input.
- Do **not** introduce new information or alter the meaning of the original query.
- Ensure that the rewritten query is **semantically equivalent** and **syntactically correct**.

#### 4. **Ensure Consistency in Placeholders**
- If the query contains multiple instances of the same type of PII, use the **same placeholder** (e.g., use [Company] for all company names).
- Replace any existing placeholders (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`) with your chosen placeholder (e.g., [Email]).

#### 5. **Review the Rewritten Query**
- Review the rewritten text to ensure **clarity**, **consistency**, and that the **original intent is preserved**.
- Ensure that the rewritten query is **not only anonymized** but also **semantically and syntactically equivalent** to the original.

---

### Domain-Specific Notes:
- **Companies, organizations, and universities** may be named in the query and should be replaced with [Company], [Organization], or [University] depending on context.
- **Dates** may appear in various formats (e.g., "April 19", "DEC 15th/2023") and should be replaced with [Date].
- **Emails** may be anonymized already (e.g., `<PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_EMAIL_ADDRESS>`) and should be replaced with [Email].
- **Names** may appear in full or partial form (e.g., "Salar", "Waqas", "May") and should be replaced with [Name].
- **Job titles or roles** (e.g., "Event Manager", "quant developer", "software engineer") should be replaced with [Position] if they are specific to the individual.
- **Document numbers** may include prefixes or identifiers (e.g., "MSN:0756") and should be replaced with [Document Number].
- **Departments or sections** (e.g., "IOCC section") should be replaced with [Department].

---

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use a **consistent and standardized placeholder system** across all PII types.
- **Preserve the grammatical structure** and **original intent** of the query.
- **Avoid introducing any new information or assumptions** not present in the original query.
- Ensure that the rewritten query is **not only anonymized** but also **semantically and syntactically equivalent** to the original.

---

### Examples:
#### Input:
"I have a business named Shumti and Co, that is an opticians shop with bespoke frames from special brands."

#### Output:
"I have a business named [Company], that is an opticians shop with bespoke frames from special brands."

#### Input:
"We are a global platform established as an LLC in 2021. Our main office is in Cairo, Egypt."

#### Output:
"We are a global platform established as an LLC in [Date]. Our main office is in [Location], [Country]."

---

### Key Considerations:
- **Avoid overgeneralization or under-identification** of PII. Be thorough in scanning for all possible PII types.
- **Maintain the original tone** (e.g., formal, casual, technical) of the query.
- **Ensure that placeholders are clearly marked** and **do not resemble real data** (e.g., [Name], not [John] or [Jane]).

---

### Final Review:
- Check that all PII has been replaced with the correct placeholder.
- Ensure the rewritten query is **clear**, **consistent**, and **semantically equivalent**.
- Ensure that the rewritten query is **grammatically correct** and **structurally similar** to the original.
